         <!-- Description -->
         <div class="col-md-6 col-md-pull-3 col-xs-12 col-description">
          <div class="hidden-sm hidden-xs">
           <div class="product-title">
            <h1>
             SparkFun Inventor's Kit for Arduino (Old Stock)
            </h1>
            <div class="sku">
             KIT-10173
             <span class="product-icons">
              <a data-toggle="notify" href="https://www.sparkfun.com/static/rohs/">
               <span class="rohs">
                RoHS
                <span class="glyphicon glyphicon-ok">
                </span>
               </span>
              </a>
             </span>
             <br/>
             <a href="#reviews">
             </a>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="description" itemprop="description">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Description:
            </strong>
            <strong>
             Replacement:
            </strong>
            <a href="https://www.sparkfun.com/products/11227">
             KIT-11227
            </a>
            . Weve overhauled the SIK Manual with new graphics, revised code and in-depth instruction! Also, the kit includes a red translucent breadboard instead of the clear one which some found visually confusing, and the new and improved baseplate! This page is for reference only.
           </p>
           <p>
            zOMG! This kit has it all. It includes the Arduino Uno, the fabled baseplate, and all the sensors you can shake a stick at. The SparkFun Inventors Kit for Arduino is a box of goodies to get the very beginner started with programmable electronics. It includes all the bits you need to build 14 basic circuits, no soldering required! On top of that, weve joined forces with Oomlout to offer a small booklet to get you started. The SIK comes with everything pictured and a 36 page color printed starter guide. The guide will take a complete novice and get them:
           </p>
           <ul>
            <li>
             Blinking LEDs
            </li>
            <li>
             Controlling a toy motor
            </li>
            <li>
             Controlling a servo
            </li>
            <li>
             Making (bad) music
            </li>
            <li>
             Responding to buttons
            </li>
            <li>
             Twisting a volume knob
            </li>
            <li>
             Detecting ambient light
            </li>
            <li>
             Reading temperature
            </li>
            <li>
             Controlling big devices
            </li>
            <li>
             Mixing LED colors
            </li>
           </ul>
           <p>
            We believe these to be the building blocks of any electronics project. Once these concepts are mastered, very impressive projects are possible using simple recombinations.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Note:
            </strong>
            No soldering required. We recommend this kit for beginners ages 10 and up.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Note:
            </strong>
            Because Atmel is moving more and more of their production capacity to surface mount ICs, the DIP packaged ATmega328 is becoming more and more difficult to get. To keep up with demand, we now offer the Arduino Uno with an SMD ATmega328. The board is identical to the PTH version of the Uno, but you wont be able to remove the ATmega328 without some hot-air. This change shouldnt affect most users.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Note:
            </strong>
            There is an error with CIRC-03. Omit the 10K resistor and hook pin 9 directly to the base of the transistor.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Note:
            </strong>
            This product is a collaboration with Oomlout. A portion of each sales goes back to them for product support and continued development.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Kit includes:
            </strong>
           </p>
           <ul>
            <li>
             <a href="https://www.sparkfun.com/products/11224">
              Arduino Uno SMD R3
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="https://www.sparkfun.com/products/11235">
              Arduino and breadboard holder
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/tutorial/AIK/ARDX-EG-SPAR-PRINT-85-REV-10.pdf">
              Printed 36-page Oomlout manual
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/tutorial/AIK/CIRC00-sheet-SPAR.pdf">
              12 color circuit overlays
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=9567">
              Clear Bread Board
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=733">
              74HC595 Shift Register
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             2N2222 Transistors
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/products/8588">
              1N4148 Diodes
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/products/10171">
              DC Motor with wires
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=9065">
              Small Servo
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=100">
              5V Relay
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/products/10988">
              TMP36 Temp Sensor
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/products/10264">
              Flex sensor
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=8680">
              Softpot
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=513">
              6' USB Cable
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/products/11026">
              Jumper Wires
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=9088">
              Photocell
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=105">
              Tri-color LED
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=9590">
              Red
             </a>
             and
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/products/532">
              Yellow
             </a>
             LEDs
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=9806">

             </a>
            </li>

             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=9190">
              Big 12mm Buttons
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=8377">
              330
             </a>
             and
             <a href="http://www.sparkfun.com/commerce/product_info.php?products_id=8374">
              10K
             </a>
             Resistors
            </li>

              Male Headers
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Documentation:
            </strong>
           </p>
           <ul>

             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://ryanwaggoner.com/2010/10/damn-you-arduino-i-have-no-free-time-for-this/">
              SIK Review
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://learn.sparkfun.com/resources/SIK%20Binder/">
              SIK Education Binder
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://sprkfn.com/w29376">
              Parts Wishlist
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="http://cdn.sparkfun.com/datasheets/Dev/Arduino/Boards/SparkFunInventorsKit.zip">
              Example Code
             </a>

              <div class="main">
               <span class="is_recommended">
                <span class="sfe-icon-flame">
                </span>
                SparkFun Recommended
               </span>
               <h3 class="title">
                <a href="https://www.sparkfun.com/products/11021" itemprop="url">
                 <span itemprop="name">
                  Arduino Uno - R3
                 </span>
                </a>
               </h3>
               <span class="bubbles" style="display:none">
                <a data-toggle="notify" href="https://www.sparkfun.com/static/bubbles/" title="in stock">
                 <span class="sfe-icon-stock-in">
                  <span class="visuallyhidden">
                   In stock
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </a>
               </span>
               <span class="sku" itemprop="sku">
                DEV-11021
               </span>
               <p class="description" itemprop="description" style="display:none">
                This is the new Arduino Uno R3. In addition to all the features of the previous board, the Uno now uses an ATmega16U2 instead

                   <div class="comment-info">
                    <div class="avatar">

                    <a class="alias" href="https://www.sparkfun.com/users/314013">

                    <span class="date" title="Sunday, 01-Apr-12 23:13:28 MDT">
                     <a href="https://www.sparkfun.com/products/retired/10173#comment-4f793578ce395f1771000000">
                      about 3 years ago
                     </a>
                    </span>
                    <span class="wide">
                     /
                    </span>
                    <span class="rating-star">
                     <span class="star-dark" title="Please log in to up-vote comments">
                      <span class="sfe-icon-star-full">
                      </span>
                     </span>
                    </span>
                    <span class="rating" id="comment-rating-4f793578ce395f1771000000">
                     3
                    </span>
                    <div class="actions">
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="comment-text">
                    <p>
                     Wish Id read this earlier, but I did diagnose - and fix - the problem.
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     Yes, the motor draws more current than the circuit (as shown) supplies.   It works if you swap the 10k resistor (which limits the current from pin 9 to the transistor base) for a 1k resistor.  The transistor isnt switching all the way on with the tiny current the 10k lets through.  It will work with some low current motors (I got it to work with a tiny motor at 20ma) but not the bigger one with the kit.
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     The kit doesnt come  with 1k resistors.  The value isnt too critical, so if you dont have one handy you can use  330 ohm resistors in series (at least 2, for 660 ohms) or three 10k in parallel (3.3k) to get into the right ballpark.  (You need enough resistance to prevent burning out the pin from too much current draw.)
                    </p>
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </li>

                  <p>
                   Hi cap9qd -
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   I got this kit for my son (age 11) and the two of us have been working through the circuits together. We love it - though we hit exactly the same problem you did last week w/the motor circuit and solved the same way with the help of a community member, by dropping the resistor down, in our case to 330 ohm, which worked fine.
                  </p>
                 </div>
                </div>

                 <div class="comment-text">
                  <p>
                   I got this for my father for Christmas.  He was working through the lessons and got stumped on the one where you run the little DC motor (Lesson CIRC-03).  After finding a bad jumper wire we still couldnt get it to work.  Changed the motor to an LED and resistor to verify the transistor circuit worked and it did.  Finally had to replace the transistor base resistor from a 10k to 1k to get enough collector current to run the motor.  Hope this helps someone else who has issues.
                  </p>
                 </div>

                   <div class="comment-text">
                    <p>
                     the 2N3904 is a close replacement NPN BJT transistor replacement to the 2N2222. I think the 2N3904 can only handle a third of the current or something. http://www.sparkfun.com/products/521
                     <br/>
                     For temperature, I use a thermistor on my UNO and it worked great. http://www.sparkfun.com/products/250 and the arduino code: http://www.arduino.cc/playground/ComponentLib/Thermistor
                    </p>
                   </div>

                     <br/>
                     int main()  {
                     <br/>
                     int wait_time;
                     <br/>
                     int return_value;
                     <br/>
                     wait_time=60;
                     <br/>
                     while (go_check_your_email() == NOT_SHIPPED_YET)   {
                     <br/>
                     sleep(wait_time);
                     <br/>

                 <div class="comment-text">
                  <p>
                   I got one of these that included 1N4148 instead of the listed 1N4001 diodes. Which is it? Customer service says 1N4148, but this page says 1N4001. I got tired of arguing with Customer service and pointing to this page while they pointed to the manufacturing floor. I think these will work for the experiments in the guide, but cmon  &lt;br /&gt;
                   <br/>
                   &lt;br /&gt;
                   <br/>
                   Even though they kindly sent me a replacement diode, another 1N4148 I figured how much is a 15cent part worth fighting for? Moral - be sure to check your part numbers to the packing list and be prepared for a trip to the Shack or adding more hearty diodes to your Digi-key order.&lt;br /&gt;
                   <br/>
                   &lt;br /&gt;
                   <br/>
                   Its the details that matter.
                  </p>

                   </div>
                   <div class="comment-text">
                    <p>
                     Id tried tinkering with picaxe years ago, but after building the little board from a pen-drawn circuit sketch, and finally blinking an LED, I found myself in a, Ok so now what? situation, and abandoned it.  I hadnt actually learned much.
                     <br/>
                     Less than a year ago I bought this kit.  The amount of consideration that went into this thing is amazing.  That simple little project booklet and circuit overlays are great.  Things clicked, and now I do all kinds of fun and useful things with various mcus, my own boards, etc.  It was the perfect launch pad to a whole new hobby.
                     <br/>
                     I might be a bit beyond one now, but if Id known of a formal follow-on kit I almost certainly would have purchased it.  Maybe something that dealt with voltage dividers, using additional libraries, maybe throw in that inexpensive dmm, etc.  Does SFE have something like that?
                     <br/>
                     Anyways, thanks!  My nephews are definitely going to inherit this kit.  Theyre going to love it.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                  </div>

                 <div class="comment-text">
                  <p>
                   I got a sample of this kit at the recent DC Science and Engineering Festival.  Its totally cool.  I showed it to the kids on my robotics team and they started salivating.  I sent it home with one kid. a programmer with minimal hardware experience.  He brought it back the next day having completed the first two projects (started telling me how fast he got the LED blinking:)
                   <br/>
                   His only negative comment was that the two-pin headers that are used to hold down the paper overlays were missing.  I checked the kit myself and found two 40-pin headers.  I guess the instructions didnt give him permission to cut them appart. D'oh!
                   <br/>
                   Looking forward to some fun electronics sessions with the team.
                   <br/>
                   Philbot
                  </p>

        <p>
         <b>
          SparkFun
         </b>
         is an online retail store that sells the bits and pieces to
        make your electronics projects possible. Whether it's a robot that can
        cook your breakfast or a GPS cat tracking device, our products and
        resources are designed to make the world of electronics more accessible.
        </p>
        <p>
         In addition to products, SparkFun also offers
        classes and online tutorials to help educate
        individuals in the wonderful world of embedded electronics.
        </p>
